  *...The Everlasting No had said: "Behold, thou art fatherless, outcast, and the universe
is mine (the Decil`s)" to which my whole ME now made answer:
  "I am not thine, but FREE, and forever thee!"
  It is from this hour that I incline to date my spiritual New-birth, or
Baphometic Fire-baptism: perhaps I directly therenpon began to be a Man.

  (But dropt on beds of amaranth and moly,
  How sweet (while warm airs lull us, blowing lowly)
  With half-dropped eyelid still,
  Beneath a heaven dark and holy,
  Tl watch the bright river drawing slowly
  His waters from the purple hill-
  To hear the dewy echoes calling
  From cave to cave thro` the thick-twin`d vine-
  To watch the emerald-colour`d water falling
  Thro` many a wov`n a acanthus-wreath divine!
  Only to hear and see the far-off sparkling brine!
  Only to hear were sweet, stretch`d out beneath the pine.)

  We are not now that strength which in old days
  Moved earth and heaven: that which we are, we are:
  One equal temper of heroic hearts,
  Made weak by time and fate, but strong in will
  To strive, to seek, to find, and not to hield.) 뻶 퇬?래 칊?랭톩

  And the day`s at the morn;
  Morning`s at seven
  The hill-side`s dew-pearl`d;
  The lark`s on the wing:
  The snail`s of the thorn:

  (Then love me, Love! Look on me-breathe on me:
  As brighter ladies do not count it strange,
  For love, to give up asres and degree,
  I yield the grave for thy sake, and exchange
  My neat sweet view of Heaven, for earth with thee.)

  쨒늏츞래 퇫늝톩 쵡뎮씉
  (The Sea of Faith
  Wax once, too, at the folds of a bright girdle furl`d.
  But now I only hear
  Its melancholy, long, withdrawing roar,
  Retreating, to the breath
  Of the night-wind, down the vast edges drear
  And naked shingles of the world.)
  (Dover Beach)
  땇톩 헊봺 덆퇬 期톏 떬래 렀밻 ?밻 Tristram and Iseult(1852)*돝 책뒃 Clough톩
틓톛톓 몼쐛? elegy Thyrsis(1867), The Scholar Gipsy(1853), Dover Beach
(1867), The Forsaken Merman(1849), The Church of Brou,
Stanza from the Grande Chartreus돝 Obermann, Rugby Chapel(1867)** 뾵래봞.
* The air of the december night
  Steals coldly around the chamber bright,
  Where those lifeless lover be:
  Swinging with it, in the light
  Flaps the ghostlike tapestry.
  ** What is the course of life
  Of mortal men on the earth?-
  Most men eddy about
  Here and there-eat and drink,
  Chatter and love and hate,
  Gather and squander, are raised
  Alfot, are hurl`d in the dust,
  Striving blindly achiecing
  Nothing; and no one asks
  Who of what they have been
  More than he asks what waves,
  In the moonlight solitudes mild
  Of the midmost Ocean, have swell`d
  Foam`d for a moment, and gone.

  (The blessed damozel leaned out
  from the gold bar of Heaven:
  Of waters stilled at even:
  She had three lilies in her hand
  And the stars in her hair were seven...
  It was the rampart of God`s house
  That she was standing on:
  By God biilt over the sheer depth
  The which is Space begun:
  So high, that looking downward thence
  She scarce could see the sun)

The Earthly Paradise(1868-70)** 뾵 땇톩 　뾢 덆퇬킕 뻶엨 칊죂 렀봞.
  * I know a little garden close
  Set thick with lilyand red rose,
  Where I would wander if I might
  From dewy dawn to dewy night,
  And have one with me wandering.)
  ** Forget six counties overhung with smoke,
  Forget the snotirng steam and pistons stroke,
  Forget the spreading of the hideous town;
  Think rather of the pack-horse on the down,
  and dream of London, small and white, and clean,
  The clear Thames bordered by its gardens green;
  Think that below bridge the green lapping waves
  Smite some few keels that bear Levantine staves...

  Through the kisses that blossom and bud,
  By the lips intertwisted and birren

  By the hands as they slacken and strain,

  And in the osier-isle we heard them noise,
  We has not to look back on summer joys,
  Or forward to a summer of bright dye:...
  Love, that had robbed us of immortal things,
  This littke moment mercifully gave,
  Where I have been across the twilight wave
  The swan sail with her young beneath her wings...

  That Youth`s sweet-scented manuscript should close!

  Ah whence, and whither flown again, who knows!...
  Ah Love! could you and I with Him conspire

  My task which I am trying to achieve is, by the power of the written word, to
make you hear, to make you feel-it is, before all, to make you see. That-and no
more, and it is everything. If I succeed, you shall find there according to your
deserts: encouragement, consolation, fear, charm- all you demand, and, perhaps,
also that glimpse of truth for which you have forgotten to ask.
